> Analysis of Algorithms - Review
>
>  Examples of **primitive operations**:
>
>  Evaluating an expression
>
>  Assigning a value to a variable
>
>  Indexing into an array
>
>  Calling a method
>
>  Returning from a method
>
>  Evaluate f(n) in terms of **Big-Oh Notation**:
>
> ***f*(*n*)** is ***O***(***g***(***n***)) if there are positive
> constants ***c*** and ***n*0** such that

***f***(***n***) ***cg***(***n***) for ***n*** ***n*0**

>  **Asymptotic analysis**:
>
>  find the worst-case number of primitive operations executed as a
>
> function of the input size f(n)
>
>  express this function with big-Oh notation

4

![](vertopal_c04aae72e96e4a9f83baf543a6b0dcda/media/image1.png){width="8.333333333333333e-2in"
height="8.333333333333333e-2in"}![](vertopal_c04aae72e96e4a9f83baf543a6b0dcda/media/image1.png){width="8.333333333333333e-2in"
height="8.333333333333333e-2in"}![](vertopal_c04aae72e96e4a9f83baf543a6b0dcda/media/image1.png){width="8.333333333333333e-2in"

| 333333333333333e-2in" |                       |                       |
| height="8.3           |                       |                       |
| 33333333333333e-2in"} |                       |                       |
+=======================+=======================+=======================+
|                       | 1\.                   | > One or more         |
|                       |                       | > stopping            |
|                       |                       | > conditions: under   |
|                       |                       | > certain             |
+-----------------------+-----------------------+-----------------------+
|                       | > conditions, it      |                       |
|                       | > would stop the      |                       |
|                       | > method from calling |                       |
|                       | > itself again        |                       |
|                       | >                     |                       |
|                       | > This is known as   |                       |
|                       | > **base case**       |                       |
+-----------------------+-----------------------+-----------------------+
|                       | 2\.                   | > One or more         |
|                       |                       | > recursive calls:    |
|                       |                       | > this is when **a    |
|                       |                       | > method**            |
+-----------------------+-----------------------+-----------------------+
|                       | > **calls itself**\   |                       |
|                       | > These are known as |                       |
|                       | > **recursive cases** |                       |
+-----------------------+-----------------------+-----------------------+

> The recursive cases must eventually **lead to a base** **case**.
>
> Recursion 8

> Each **recursive call** should be defined so that it **makes progress
> towards a base case**.

+-----------------+-----------------+-----------------+-----------------+
| > Recursion    | > Example      |                 | **final         |
| > trace         |                 |                 | answer**        |
+=================+=================+=================+=================+
| > A box for    | **call**        | > **return 4\*6 |                 |
| > each          |                 | > = 24**        |                 |
+-----------------+-----------------+-----------------+-----------------+
| recursive call  |                 |                 |                 |
+-----------------+-----------------+-----------------+-----------------+

> An arrow from each caller to callee
>
> An arrow from each callee to caller\
> **showing return**\
> **value**
>
> **recursiveFactorial(4)**
>
> **call** **return 3\*2 = 6 recursiveFactorial(3)**
>
> **call return 2\*1 = 2 recursiveFactorial(2)**
>
> **call** **return 1\*1 = 1 recursiveFactorial(1)**
>
> **call** **return 1**
>
> **recursiveFactorial(0)**

|             | if (n == 0) | > //**base  |             |             |
|             |             | > case**    |             |             |
+-------------+-------------+-------------+-------------+-------------+

|             | > case**:   |             |             |             |
|             | > the       |             |             |             |
|             | > parameter |             |             |             |
|             | > is **n**  |             |             |             |
|             | > and the   |             |             |             |
|             | > recursive |             |             |             |
|             | > call      |             |             |             |
|             | > passes // |             |             |             |
|             | > the       |             |             |             |
|             | > argument  |             |             |             |
|             | > **n −     |             |             |             |
|             | > 1**\      |             |             |             |
|             | > return (n |             |             |             |
|             | > \*        |             |             |             |
|             | > factorial |             |             |             |
|             | > (n -- 1)) |             |             |             |

> mid = (n-1)/𝟐𝒌≥**1** →**(n-1)** ≥2𝑘→**n** ≥2𝑘→ **log(n)** ≥**k
> log(2)** →**log(n)** ≥**k**
>
> Hence, there can be **at most log n levels**
>
> Recursion 17

| ![](vertopal_c04aae72e96e4a9      | > Test for base cases            |
| f83baf543a6b0dcda/media/image1.pn | >                                 |
| g){width="8.333333333333333e-2in" | > Begin by testing for a set of  |
| height="8.333333333333333e-2in"}  | > **base cases** (there should be |
|                                   | > at least one).                  |
| ![](vertopal_c04aae72e96e4a9      | >                                 |
| f83baf543a6b0dcda/media/image1.pn | > Every possible chain of        |
| g){width="8.333333333333333e-2in" | > recursive calls must eventually |
| height="8.333333333333333e-2in"}  | > **reach a base case**, and the  |
|                                   | > handling of each base case      |
| ![](vertopal_c04aae72e96e4a9      | > should not use recursion.       |
| f83baf543a6b0dcda/media/image1.pn | >                                 |
| g){width="8.333333333333333e-2in" | > Recur once                     |
| height="8.333333333333333e-2in"}  | >                                 |
|                                   | > Perform **a single recursive   |
| ![](vertopal_c04aae72e96e4a9      | > call**                          |
| f83baf543a6b0dcda/media/image1.pn | >                                 |
| g){width="8.333333333333333e-2in" | > This step may have a test that |
| height="8.333333333333333e-2in"}  | > decides which of several        |
|                                   | > possible recursive calls to     |
| ![](vertopal_c04aae72e96e4a9      | > make, but it should ultimately  |
| f83baf543a6b0dcda/media/image1.pn | > make just one of these calls    |
| g){width="8.333333333333333e-2in" |                                   |
| height="8.333333333333333e-2in"}  |                                   |
|                                   |                                   |
| ![](vertopal_c04aae72e96e4a9      |                                   |
| f83baf543a6b0dcda/media/image1.pn |                                   |
| g){width="8.333333333333333e-2in" |                                   |
| height="8.333333333333333e-2in"}  |                                   |

| ![](vertopal_c04aae72e96e4a9      | factorial **function definition  |

| g){width="8.333333333333333e-2in" |                                   |
| height="8.333333333333333e-2in"}  | > In file systems the **data     |
|                                   | > structure is recursive**,       |

| ![](vertopal_c04aae72e96e4a9      | > smaller instance and then the   |
| f83baf543a6b0dcda/media/image1.pn | > **base case** lies at the       |
| g){width="8.333333333333333e-2in" | > bottom, guaranteeing the        |
| height="8.333333333333333e-2in"}  | > convergence.                    |

> with more examples.

height="8.333333333333333e-2in"}![](vertopal_c04aae72e96e4a9f83baf543a6b0dcda/media/image22.png){width="4.316666666666666in"
height="2.069274934383202in"}![](vertopal_c04aae72e96e4a9f83baf543a6b0dcda/media/image23.png){width="10.0in"
height="7.5in"}

![](vertopal_c04aae72e96e4a9f83baf543a6b0dcda/media/image1.png){width="8.333333333333333e-2in"
height="8.333333333333333e-2in"}

> Example of Linear Recursion
>
> Algorithm linearSum(A, n): Input:\
> Array, A, of integers\
> Integer n such that\
> 0 ≤ n ≤ \|A\|\
> Output:\
> Sum of the first **n**\
> integers in A
>
> Example: data = \[4, 3, 6, 2, 8\], n=5\
> The **sum can be expressed recursively** as the sum of n-1 elements
> plus the last one.
>
> if n = 0 then\
> return 0\
> else\
> return\
> linearSum(A, n - 1) + A\[n - 1\]

+-----------------------+-----------------------+-----------------------+
| > © 2014 Goodrich,    | > Recursion           | 23                    |
| > Tamassia,           |                       |                       |
| > Goldwasser          |                       |                       |
+=======================+=======================+=======================+
+-----------------------+-----------------------+-----------------------+

<th colspan="20"><blockquote>
<p>The power function, p(x,n)=xn, can be <strong>defined
recursively</strong>:</p>
</blockquote></th>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<th rowspan="2"><em>p</em></th>
<th rowspan="2">(</th>
<th rowspan="2"><em>x</em></th>
<th rowspan="2">,</th>
<th rowspan="2"><em>n</em></th>
<th rowspan="2">)</th>
<th rowspan="2">=</th>
<th rowspan="2"><blockquote>
<p>ìíî</p>
</blockquote></th>
<th rowspan="2"><em>x</em></th>
<th rowspan="2">×<em>p</em></th>
<th rowspan="2">(</th>
<th colspan="2">1</th>
<th rowspan="2"><em>n</em></th>
<th rowspan="2">-</th>
<th rowspan="2"><blockquote>
<p>1 )</p>
</blockquote></th>
<th rowspan="2">if</th>
<th><em>n</em></th>
<th>=</th>
<th rowspan="2"><blockquote>
<p>0</p>
</blockquote></th>
</tr>
<tr class="header">
<th><em>x</em></th>
<th>,</th>
<th colspan="2">else</th>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<th colspan="20"><blockquote>
<p>For example: 𝑝𝑥, 3 = 𝑥3= 𝑥∙𝑥2</p>
</blockquote></th>
</tr>

> This leads to a power function that runs in O(n) time (for we make
> **n** recursive calls)We can do better than this, however

<th colspan="29"><blockquote>
<p>We can derive a more efficient linearly<br />
recursive algorithm by using repeated squaring:</p>
</blockquote></th>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<th rowspan="3"><em>p</em></th>
<th rowspan="3">(</th>
<th rowspan="3"><em>x</em></th>
<th rowspan="3">,</th>
<th rowspan="3"><em>n</em></th>
<th rowspan="3">)</th>
<th rowspan="3"></th>
<th rowspan="3"><blockquote>
<p></p>
</blockquote>
<p></p></th>
<th rowspan="3"><em>x</em></th>
<th rowspan="3"></th>
<th rowspan="2"><em>p</em></th>
<th rowspan="2">(</th>
<th rowspan="2"><em>x</em></th>
<th rowspan="2">,</th>
<th rowspan="2">(</th>
<th>1</th>
<th rowspan="2"></th>
<th rowspan="2">1 )</th>
<th rowspan="2">/</th>
<th rowspan="3">2 )</th>
<th rowspan="3"><blockquote>
<p>2</p>
</blockquote></th>
<th rowspan="2">if</th>
<th colspan="2">if</th>
<th><em>x</em></th>
<th colspan="2"></th>
<th colspan="2"><blockquote>
<p>0</p>
</blockquote></th>
</tr>
<tr class="header">
<th><em>n</em></th>
<th><em>x</em></th>
<th></th>
<th colspan="2">0</th>
<th colspan="2">is</th>
<th><blockquote>
<p>odd</p>
</blockquote></th>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<th colspan="2"><em>p</em></th>
<th>(</th>
<th><em>x</em></th>
<th>,</th>
<th><em>n</em></th>
<th>/</th>
<th>2 )</th>
<th>2</th>
<th>if</th>
<th><em>x</em></th>
<th></th>
<th>0</th>
<th colspan="2">is</th>
<th colspan="2"><blockquote>
<p>even</p>
</blockquote></th>
</tr>
<tr class="header">
<th colspan="29"><blockquote>
<p>For example,</p>
<p>24= 2(4<em>/</em>2)2 = (24<em>/</em>2)2 = (22)2 = 42 = 16<br />
25= 21+(4<em>/</em>2)2 = 2(24<em>/</em>2)2 = 2(22)2 = 2(42) = 32 26=
2(6<em>/</em> 2)2 = (26<em>/</em>2)2 = (23)2 = 82 = 64<br />
27= 21+(6<em>/</em>2)2 = 2(26<em>/</em>2)2 = 2(23)2 = 2(82) = 128</p>
</blockquote></th>
</tr>

+=======================+=======================+=======================+
|                       | **if** n = 0          | > **then**            |
+-----------------------+-----------------------+-----------------------+
|                       | > **return** 1\       |                       |
|                       | > **if** n is odd     |                       |
|                       | > **then**\           |                       |
|                       | > y = Power(x, (n -   |                       |
|                       | > 1)/ 2) **return** x |                       |
|                       | > · y ·y\             |                       |
|                       | > **else**            |                       |
+-----------------------+-----------------------+-----------------------+

> y = Power(x, n/ 2)\
> **return** y · y

+-----------------------+-----------------------+-----------------------+
| > © 2014 Goodrich,    | > Recursion           | 29                    |
| > Tamassia,           |                       |                       |
| > Goldwasser          |                       |                       |
+=======================+=======================+=======================+
+-----------------------+-----------------------+-----------------------+

+-----------------------------------+-----------------------------------+
| ![](vertopal_c04aae72e96e4a9      | > Analysis                        |
| f83baf543a6b0dcda/media/image1.pn |                                   |
| g){width="8.333333333333333e-2in" |                                   |
| height="8.333333333333333e-2in"}  |                                   |
+===================================+===================================+
+-----------------------------------+-----------------------------------+

> **Algorithm** Power(x, n):\
> **Input:** A number x and integer n = 0\
> **Output:** The value xn\
> **if** n = 0 **then**\
> **return** 1\
> **if** n is odd **then**\
> y = Power(x, (n - 1)/ 2) **return** x · y · y\
> **else**\
> y = Power(x, n/ 2)\
> **return** y · y
>
> Each time we make a\
> recursive call we halve the value of n; hence, we make log n recursive
> calls. That is, this\
> method runs in O(log n) time.
>
> It is important that we use a variable twice\
> here rather than calling the method twice.

+-----------------------+-----------------------+-----------------------+
| > © 2014 Goodrich,    | > Recursion           | 30                    |
| > Tamassia,           |                       |                       |
| > Goldwasser          |                       |                       |
+=======================+=======================+=======================+
+-----------------------+-----------------------+-----------------------+

| ![](            | > Tail         |                 |                 |
| vertopal_c04aae | > recursion     |                 |                 |
| 72e96e4a9f83baf | > occurs when a |                 |                 |
| 543a6b0dcda/med | > linearly      |                 |                 |
| ia/image1.png){ | > recursive     |                 |                 |
| width="8.333333 | > method makes  |                 |                 |
| 333333333e-2in" | > its           |                 |                 |
| he              | > **recursive   |                 |                 |
| ight="8.3333333 | > call as its   |                 |                 |
| 33333333e-2in"} | > last          |                 |                 |
|                 | > step**.The   |                 |                 |
| ![](            | > **array       |                 |                 |
| vertopal_c04aae | > reversal**    |                 |                 |
| 72e96e4a9f83baf | > method is an  |                 |                 |
| 543a6b0dcda/med | > example.      |                 |                 |
| ia/image1.png){ | >               |                 |                 |
| width="8.333333 | > Such methods |                 |                 |
| 333333333e-2in" | > can be easily |                 |                 |
| he              | > converted to  |                 |                 |
| ight="8.3333333 | > non-\         |                 |                 |
| 33333333e-2in"} | > recursive     |                 |                 |
|                 | > methods       |                 |                 |
| ![](            | > (which saves  |                 |                 |
| vertopal_c04aae | > on some       |                 |                 |
| 72e96e4a9f83baf | > resources).   |                 |                 |

| ight="8.3333333 | > i, j ):\      |                 |                 |

| ight="8.3333333 | > index i and   |                 |                 |
| 33333333e-2in"} | > ending at j\  |                 |                 |

> amount of additional space, whereas linearSum uses O(n)

+=================+=================+=================+=================+
|                 | > *F*0 = 0\     | > \+ *Fi-*2     | > for *i \>* 1. |
|                 | > *F*1 = 1\     |                 |                 |
|                 | > *Fi* = *Fi-*1 |                 |                 |
+-----------------+-----------------+-----------------+-----------------+
|                 | > Recursive    |                 |                 |
|                 | > algorithm     |                 |                 |
|                 | > (first        |                 |                 |
|                 | > attempt):     |                 |                 |
|                 | > **Algorithm** |                 |                 |
|                 | > B             |                 |                 |
|                 | inaryFib(*k*):\ |                 |                 |
|                 | > ***Input:***  |                 |                 |
|                 | > Nonnegative   |                 |                 |
|                 | > integer *k*\  |                 |                 |
|                 | > ***Output:*** |                 |                 |
|                 | > The *k*th     |                 |                 |
|                 | > Fibonacci     |                 |                 |
|                 | > number *Fk*   |                 |                 |
|                 | > **if** *k* ≤1 |                 |                 |
|                 | > **then**\     |                 |                 |
|                 | > **return**    |                 |                 |
|                 | > *k*\          |                 |                 |
|                 | > **else**      |                 |                 |
+-----------------+-----------------+-----------------+-----------------+

**return** BinaryFib(*k* 1) + BinaryFib(*k* 2)

+-----------------------+-----------------------+-----------------------+
| > © 2014 Goodrich,    | > Recursion           | 41                    |
| > Tamassia,           |                       |                       |
| > Goldwasser          |                       |                       |

> Algorithm for Multiple Recursion
>
> **Algorithm** PuzzleSolve(k,S,U):\
> **Input:** Integer k, sequence S, and set U (universe of elements to
> test)\
> **Output:** Enumeration of all k-length extensions to S using elements
> in U without repetitions\
> **for all** e in U **do**\
> Remove e from U {e is now being used}\
> Add e to the end of S\
> **if** k = 1 **then**\
> Test whether S is a configuration that solves the puzzle **if** S
> solves the puzzle **then**\
> **return** "Solution found: " S\
> **else**\
> PuzzleSolve(k - 1, S,U)\
> Add e back to U\
> {e is now unused} Remove e from the end of S

© 2014 Goodrich, Tamassia, Goldwasser Recursion 45

+========+========+========+========+========+========+========+========+
|        | >      |        | neces  |        |        |        |        |
|        |  799 + |        | sarily |        |        |        |        |
|        | > 98 = |        | in     |        |        |        |        |
|        | > 997  |        | that   |        |        |        |        |
|        |        |        | order  |        |        |        |        |
+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+
|        | \[\]   |        |        |        |        |        |        |
|        | {      |        |        |        |        |        |        |
|        | a,b,c} |        |        |        |        |        |        |
+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+
|        | \[a\]  |        | >      |        |        | >      |        |
|        | {b,c}  |        |  \[b\] |        |        |  \[c\] |        |
|        |        |        | >      |        |        | >      |        |
|        |        |        |  {a,c} |        |        |  {a,b} |        |
+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+
|        | a=7    |        | > b=7  |        | > c=7  |        |        |
+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+
|        | \[ab\] | >      | \[ca\] |        |        |        | >      |
|        | {c}    | \[ac\] | {b}    |        |        |        | \[cb\] |
|        |        | > {b}  |        |        |        |        | > {a}  |
+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+
|        | a      | > a    | c      |        |        |        | > c    |
|        | =7,b=8 | =7,c=8 | =7,a=8 |        |        |        | =7,b=8 |
+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+
|        | c=9    | > b=9  | b=9    |        |        |        | > a=9  |
+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+
|        | \[ba\] |        |        | >      |        |        | >      |
|        | {c}    |        |        | \[bc\] |        |        |  might |
|        |        |        |        | > {a}  |        |        | > be   |
|        |        |        |        |        |        |        | > able |
|        |        |        |        |        |        |        | > to   |
+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+
|        | b      |        |        | > b    |        |        |        |
|        | =7,a=8 |        |        | =7,c=8 |        |        |        |
+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+--------+
|        | c=9    |        | a=9    |        |        |        | > stop |
|        |        |        |        |        |        |        | >      |
|        |        |        |        |        |        |        | sooner |
